        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>The Pirates acquired outfielder Jaff Decker along with right-hander Miles Mikolas from the Padres this offseason in exchange for 1B/OF Alex Dickerson. In Decker, Pittsburgh gets an extreme on-base guy who can smack the ball out of the park and run the bags. In 2009, Decker lead the Midwest League in both on-base percentage (.442) and OPS (.956), then in 2011 he lead the Texas League in walks (103). Despite his ability to get on base, <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/the-jaff-decker-travis-snider-andrew-lambo-gaby-sanchez-jerry-sands-and-jose-tabata-solution/" style="text-decoration: none;">Eno suggests</a> the Pirates have a stable of corner outfielders in the fold for Decker to compete with in Spring Training. If Decker breaks with the club, NL-Only players could consider him late in their drafts to potentially platoon against righties. (Alan Harrison)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Decker has power and patience, but he's in a crowded Pirate corner outfield / first base group. If he can hit enough for first base, he has some long-term upside, but that corner outfield spot is eventually going to be Gregory Polanco's.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Many moons ago, Jaff Decker was an intriguing prospect in the Padres system. Fast-foward about five years and sift through a handful of injuries, though, and you'll find yourself looking at a shell of that prospect. He still gets on a base a lot due to the free pass but his power output has dried up -- making him a dude that has one trick up his sleeve. It's actually pretty impressive that he still has a 40-man roster spot, given that the Pirates have at least five outfielders on the depth chart ahead of him. He doesn't turn 25 until February so he still has age on his side but he looks like a future quad-A player who will either carve out a brief niche as a pinch-hitter or who will go make a bunch of money playing in Asia. (Marc Hulet)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>If you play Japanese fantasy baseball, Decker might be a name to know in a year or two but, for now, he's not going to be on your radar unless pigs learn how to fly or the Pirates release 40% or more of their big league roster.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>A long time ago in a galaxy far, far away, Jaff Decker captivated the hearts of saberists by hitting an absurd .299/.442/.514 with 10 steals as a 19-year-old in A ball. Youth, average, walks, power, speed: Everything was there. However, the six years since haven't been as kind to Decker. His power didn't translate to the upper levels, and he missed time due to injury. As a result, he's only logged 72 big league plate appearances to date. Decker's still kicking around, is still just 25, and actually had a decent year in Triple-A last year. Though, plenty of other mid-20s corner outfielders also had decent years in Triple-A last year. On the bright side, Decker cut down on his strikeout rate last year. Decker can get on base, and will steal the occasional bag, but doesn't have the power to merit regular playing time. It's doubtful he'll ever be anything more than a bench player. (Chris Mitchell)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Although he's still just 25, Decker's days as a compelling prospect are far behind him. His upside is minimal enough that you can safely disregard him in fantasy.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Decker has spent parts of four seasons in the major leagues, and yet, by plate appearance total, still has his rookie qualifications. He has carved a niche out in Triple-A as a player who can get on base at a high rate, steal some bags, and get called up to the big leagues every now and then to provide some depth when the big league roster is dealing with multiple injuries. He has over 1,500 plate appearances in Triple-A while spending time with three organizations and is only now turning 27 during the offseason. He should be able to continue chasing the on-base record in Triple-A for the next few years while waiting for more cups of coffee from the big league level. (Jason Collette)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Well down the path to Triple-A lifer who continues to show impressive on-base skills that have not made it into his checked luggage when he flies to join the big league clubs.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
</table>
